                      None, QFont]:\n        self._basic_py_validation(value, str)\n        if isinstance(value, configutils.Unset):\n            return value\n        elif not value:\n            return None\n\n        style_map = {\n            'normal': QFont.StyleNormal,\n            'italic': QFont.StyleItalic,\n            'oblique': QFont.StyleOblique,\n        }\n        weight_map = {\n            'normal': QFont.Normal,\n            'bold': QFont.Bold,\n        }\n        font = QFont()\n        font.setStyle(QFont.StyleNormal)\n        font.setWeight(QFont.Normal)\n\n        match = self.font_regex.fullmatch(value)\n        if not match:  # pragma: no cover\n            # This should never happen, as the regex always matches everything\n            # as family.\n            raise configexc.ValidationError(value, \"must be a valid font\")\n\n        style = match.group('style')\n        weight = match.group('weight')\n        namedweight = match.group('namedweight')\n        size = match.group('size')\n        family = match.group('family')\n        if style:\n            font.setStyle(style_map[style])\n        if namedweight:\n            font.setWeight(weight_map[namedweight])\n        if weight:\n            # based on qcssparser.cpp:setFontWeightFromValue\n            font.setWeight(min(int(weight) // 8, 99))\n        if size:\n       size))  # pragma: no cover\n\n        if family == 'monospace' and self.monospace_fonts is not None:\n            family = self.monospace_fonts\n        # The Qt CSS parser handles \" and ' When setting from `config.py`, both a string or a `re.compile(...)` object\n    are valid.\n\n    Attributes:\n        flags: The flags to be used when a string is passed.\n        _regex_type: The Python type of a regex object.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, flags: str = None,\n                 none_ok: bool = False) -> None:\n        super().__init__(none_ok)\n        self._regex_type = type(re.compile(''))\n        # Parse flags from configdata.yml\n        if flags is None:\n            self.flags = 0\n        else:\n            self.flags = functools.reduce(\n                operator.or_,\n                (getattr(re, flag.strip()) for flag in flags.split(' | ')))\n\n    def _compile_regex(self, pattern: str) -> typing.Pattern[str]:\n        \"\"\"Check if the given regex is valid.\n\n        This is more complicated than it could be since there's a warning on\n        invalid escapes with newer Python versions, and we want to catch that\n        case and treat it as invalid.\n        \"\"\"\n        with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as recorded_warnings:\n            warnings.simplefilter('always')\n            try:\n                compiled = re.compile(pattern, self.flags)\n            except re.error as e:\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - \" + str(e))\n            except RuntimeError:  # pragma: no cover\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - recursion depth \"\n                    \"exceeded\")\n\n        assert recorded_warnings is not None\n\n        for w in recorded_warnings:\n            if (issubclass(w.category, DeprecationWarning) and\n                    str(w.message).startswith('bad escape')):\n                raise configexc.ValidationError(\n                    pattern, \"must be a valid regex - \" + str(w.message))\n            else:\n                warnings.warn(w.message)\n\n        return compiled\n\n    def to_py(\n            self,\n            value: typing.Union[str, typing.Pattern[str]]\n    ) -> typing.Union[configutils.Unset, None, {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012VyNGbPSVjhwi4emfoZPdH","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I found the bug! Looking at the `_parse_value` function (lines 1004-1018), I can see the issue:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100  # This is the problem!\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\nThe issue is that for HSV colors:\n- Hue values range from 0-359 degrees\n- Saturation and Value range from 0-255\n\nWhen parsing percentages, the code sets `mult = 255.0 / 100` for ALL components. This works for saturation and value (since they scale from 0-255), but for hue, it should scale to 0-359 degrees.\n\nSo when someone writes `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)`:\n- For hue: 100 * (255/100) = 255 (wrong! should be 100 * (359/100) = 359)\n- For saturation: 100 * (255/100) = 255 (correct)\n- For value: 100 * (255/100) = 255 (correct)\n\nAnd for `hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)`:\n- For hue: 50 * (255/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127 (wrong! should be 50 * (359/100) = 179.5 ≈ 179)\n- For saturation: 50 * (255/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127 (correct)\n\n\n- For value: 50 * (255/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127 (correct)\n\nThe core problem is that `_parse_value` lacks context about which component it's parsing, so it applies the same multiplier uniformly. I need to check what tests currently exist to understand the expected behavior better.","signature":"EuMMCkYICxgCKkDLTOZo4aQHG0aAAJEXGsZce+WnP1iQR93LNpqfz+qMU2Jl6DojhkD4RbOFNN1U70Ta4UfUgHROvBDQbxWMIWrIEgxZy3wyKbBWwJgE3kEaDGcEjhQS8/cyp9hixyIwcyJhNuXTAy4KG7xNlekCNiEvQ5iFOclbZvMMUN2DlWao90RqF/AbomzdUH5eUg78KsoLWxgdEIwUp49F0yRsDd6RijlGyfH6kkOSVTwLyQn9M5KJsDYz+Q6bgYTLuQeqAHXapRltd0wgTfSu/7KsZp1qW3PtmzIopTwB5tVM/jFIW42W28TnP1qTb01aWG2g8OGKrBudCyoxNSe3keeo3oAlMlrVhoZ/emqPKqyxB9wvEabFmMgNYymaWsQpnSIPSb+wcJODTojNlHpf8rbPfzk5ueBnHUbHG120zcxkcYdUHizelQo76Yu1qJY0o3xvxo9CUGL0aUBtN+LqbZHR8VjF7vEO54E/9+jDDLe99XQs97c+G+s8S0xc059Adz0JzVxxMYIhxhspsX8eI2wWFxEBFZrEroztnLw/rqhDvwDVjY87849kWEyBehDaWw4TMyKSzSUU/K/V8XxRsPVYQs/vMovVCu9YKpPDxZm5yM/IBUkbWHXND3AFaVEf60jiBYJQdi34w9tRce79UIePiWrds42LaWTZNWGZjbCNpaqBRtnsfxslr5yjlTkqLcttgAZMUqbhNyCl+H0ieBMX25Is8xaMmrpnhE+dptQBamTj2yhcbsaHUcBozAzL49FGtntjCUIUdGqCe+rMFpALqAEpNkbZJ+4PU9Cc4TnntPVeY9MxqbTZw+ERBhdnnJ2lLNuV1itrG8wsmUD0frWrP4dXiuYqTugkZ42lftG1K4rAsiUHnj4ahH3s7zp4pcDrpcQr3kQch094zWNF1E842z8odSMbbDTD3q2oh+8r15lraHtPTwNo2n2G2ZXoUKLffs4bi9pDpk/Dx8BkKoONqIk7b+VTFXNKzi8gh7BoOz444NE/pnuq+l81GJpPBw34HqvZLXAaj2sxbPSxYKahfjsRMAYSGLo4G1PXYmyfbZL0iv9rXhVNhyRYOkXclcRE4Di3jGO/E5+Dr6fYTe92uQJwyyU/zKxw0uSLEk9WWa13SG14N6ZrDZ0fcyLpLw/TEWr9N48iIwZ64xqPmCCNB2MXrAJXIO3HuF137YOgeRuYMiFknsPNSaGv1JemyR06wdLLEyLJ7bxglqQ6OZJbsRHkwsQfXP5XzpZD+t9uwQiPGxW9u2h7LYtL//d1N8vSJJcBGGgMoT8uc5U7sRbA9y0oOOH3QJAZSD7b3uTbyFnfsa1jHkIpGDp7vP8yWG8WJoqzIo9YUuI4qdHho+EPn2/Aip0F+U0V7ATMEz0h2dZ7IbI1xpZrUkf3P4OECorxMbH+gK5+U9Lca6mpq6mF5eSYhkwVlSKJSUoCxXNWIWdW61n8g8ZewqI4kxGokaLRsJ5vY6t0MD4kBlYvcg/31yQDUJH1g7y0oYHVb0El6IbvexQJsxjY8IjgZs4yW1Yfw/vhUZq3cIpM7xtuysWYY20fEFjx/KVB03Td3PjiNqrOcb8/SVJiIa8IVG9MF4/tgr5FBv6eC8XSWk4o3S25rZFF57g/C+Hm64V2SIjHP4CKE3DNP3pmmN2F88vWkLWgdkM47Hi4qbcm2dAuLK6UAF28Hx+6XLls2uhn20YR+7XzOvZEh+wBizD80PwR1idFt8J3ll19UEDlp54Eij37FIdHEITxqghvFYeXs4XNNEuksnmc4+LR+20WgXT3UwPvz8i4fzbS+kF9SgmJT9CdgCVEf5UJXnHTAkQAuxFBobiAX4LNOJhu8K7OB6NkBwec+/fT//YUZeqARQvyYx4TldWF8PrA1m2hYGFC+HKZacvy+bztYuFbjWRQVGsfvKjioJw/HGdj1p8aHNlRnZkKUfhGISDuvv6DSzY1lHJAMb0hyi The method applies the same scaling\n    factor (255/100) to all color components when parsing percentages,\n    but hue should be scaled with 359/100 instead.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    @pytest.fixture\n    def color_parser(self):\n        \"\"\"Create a Color config type instance.\"\"\"\n        return configtypes.QtColor()\n\n    def test_parse_value_method_scales_all_components_by_255(self, color_parser):\n        \"\"\"\n        Verify that the _parse_value method incorrectly scales all components by 255.\n\n        This is the root cause: the method doesn't distinguish between hue (which\n        should use 359) and other components (which should use 255).\n        \"\"\"\n        # What it should produce for hue (using 359 instead of 255):\n        correct_hue_value = int(float(100) * (359.0 / 100))\n        assert correct_hue_value == 359, \"Correct scaling for hue should produce 359\"\n\n        # The bug: _parse_value returns 255, but HSV hue needs 359\n        assert buggy_value != correct_hue_value, (\n            \"Buggy _parse_value scales to 255, but HSV hue should scale to 359\"\n        )\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v', '--tb=short'])\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":244,"oldLines":17,"newStart":244,"newLines":17,"lines":["         # However, the color parser incorrectly scales hue percentages using a maximum of 255 instead of 359, producing wrong hue values.\n\n## Examples of the Bug\n\n```\nCurrent (Buggy) Behavior:\n- hsv(100%, 100%, 100%) → H=254, S=254, V=254  (should be H=359, S=255, V=255)\n- hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)    → H=127, S=127, V=127  (should be H=179, S=128, V=128)\n- hsv(10%, 10%, 10%)    → H=25,  S=25,  V=25   (should be H=36,  S=25,  V=25)\n- hsva(10%, 20%, 30%, 40%) → H=25, S=51, V=76, A=102 (H should be 36, others correct)\n```\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `/app/qutebrowser/config/configtypes.py` (lines 1004-1018)\n\n**Method:** `QtColor._parse_value()`\n\nThe bug is in the `_parse_value()` method which parses color component values. When it encounters a percentage value, it applies a uniform scaling factor:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100  # ← BUG: Uses 255 for all components\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\n**The Problem:**\n- For HSV colors, the hue component ranges from 0-359 degrees\n- Saturation and value components range from 0-255\n- The `_parse_value()` method doesn't distinguish between these components\n- It always scales percentages using `255 / 100`, which is correct for S/V but wrong for H\n\n**Correct Scaling Should Be:**\n- Hue: `percentage * 359 / 100`\n- Saturation: `percentage * 255 / 100`\n- Value: `percentage * 255 / 100`\n\n## How the Color Parser Works\n\nThe color parsing flow in `QtColor.to_py()` (lines 1020-1048):\n\n1. Parses color strings like `hsv(10%, 20%, 30%)`\n2. Extracts the color type (`hsv` or `hsva`) and values\n3. Calls `_parse_value()` on each component\n4. Passes the parsed values to `QColor.fromHsv()`\n\nThe issue is that `_parse_value()` doesn't know whether it's parsing a hue, saturation, value, or other component, so it can't apply component-specific scaling.\n\n## Affected Functions\n\n- `QtColor.to_py()` - Parses color strings including HSV\n- `QssColor.to_py()` - Also uses HSV parsing for stylesheet colors\n- Both HSV and HSVA notations are affected\n\n## Known References\n\nThis bug is referenced in the existing test suite with a comment at line 1253-1255 of `/app/tests/unit/config/test_configtypes.py`:\n\n```python\n# this should be (36, 25, 25) as hue goes to 359\n# however this is consistent with Qt's CSS parser\n# https://bugreports.qt.io/browse/QTBUG-70897\n('hsv(10%,10%,10%)', QColor.fromHsv(25, 25, 25)),\n```\n\nThis indicates the bug is actually consistent with Qt's CSS parser implementation (Qt Bug QTBUG-70897), so it may be intentional compatibility behavior.\n\n## Fix Strategy (Not Implemented)\n\nTo fix this bug, the `_parse_value()` method would need to:\n\n1. Accept an optional parameter indicating the component type (hue, saturation, value, alpha, red, green, blue)\n2. Apply different scaling factors based on the component type:\n   - Hue: scale to 0-359\n   - All others: scale to 0-255\n\nAlternatively, the color parsing logic could be refactored to handle HSV percentages differently from RGB percentages, with separate parsing functions.\n\n## Test Coverage\n\nA comprehensive regression test suite has been created at `/workspace/regression_test.py` with 11 test cases covering:\n\n1. HSV percentage parsing with various percentage values (10%, 20%, 50%, 100%)\n2. HSVA percentage parsing with mixed percentages\n3. Integer HSV/HSVA values (which are unaffected)\n4. RGB percentage parsing (which works correctly despite the same scaling bug)\n5. Root cause verification of the _parse_value method\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":787,"cache_read_input_tokens":68011,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":787},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ee42211-c6f1-4ec8-9ff3-b198a35860ee","uuid":"1c0593c5-737e-4fb4-86a4-54ba036bed39"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013Wfex3Mw92ygq3TCyDiYbG","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/BUG_ANALYSIS.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ee42211-c6f1-4ec8-9ff3-b198a35860ee","uuid":"3807c53b-3033-48d0-a2c4-956ced2f707c","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/BUG_ANALYSIS.md","content":"# HSV Color Percentage Parsing Bug Analysis\n\n## Issue Summary\n\nWhen users specify colors in qutebrowser configuration using HSV (Hue-Saturation-Value) notation with percentage values, the hue component is calculated incorrectly.\n\nThe hue channel in HSV color space should have a valid range of 0-359 degrees. However, the color parser incorrectly scales hue percentages using a maximum of 255 instead of 359, producing wrong hue values.\n\n## Examples of the Bug\n\n```\nCurrent (Buggy) Behavior:\n- hsv(100%, 100%, 100%) → H=254, S=254, V=254  (should be H=359, S=255, V=255)\n- hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)    → H=127, S=127, V=127  (should be H=179, S=128, V=128)\n- hsv(10%, 10%, 10%)    → H=25,  S=25,  V=25   (should be H=36,  S=25,  V=25)\n- hsva(10%, 20%, 30%, 40%) → H=25, S=51, V=76, A=102 (H should be 36, others correct)\n```\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `/app/qutebrowser/config/configtypes.py` (lines 1004-1018)\n\n**Method:** `QtColor._parse_value()`\n\nThe bug is in the `_parse_value()` method which parses color component values. When it encounters a percentage value, it applies a uniform scaling factor:\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100  # ← BUG: Uses 255 for all components\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\n**The Problem:**\n- For HSV colors, the hue component ranges from 0-359 degrees\n- Saturation and value components range from 0-255\n- The `_parse_value()` method doesn't distinguish between these components\n- It always scales percentages using `255 / 100`, which is correct for S/V but wrong for H\n\n**Correct Scaling Should Be:**\n- Hue: `percentage * 359 / 100`\n- Saturation: `percentage * 255 / 100`\n- Value: `percentage * 255 / 100`\n\n## How the Color Parser Works\n\nThe color parsing flow in `QtColor.to_py()` (lines 1020-1048):\n\n1. Parses color strings like `hsv(10%, 20%, 30%)`\n2. Extracts the color type (`hsv` or `hsva`) and values\n3. Calls `_parse_value()` on each component\n4. Passes the parsed values to `QColor.fromHsv()`\n\nThe issue is that `_parse_value()` doesn't know whether it's parsing a hue, saturation, value, or other component, so it can't apply component-specific scaling.\n\n## Affected Functions\n\n- `QtColor.to_py()` - Parses color strings including HSV\n- `QssColor.to_py()` - Also uses HSV parsing for stylesheet colors\n- Both HSV and HSVA notations are affected\n\n## Known References\n\nThis bug is referenced in the existing test suite with a comment at line 1253-1255 of `/app/tests/unit/config/test_configtypes.py`:\n\n```python\n# this should be (36, 25, 25) as hue goes to 359\n# however this is consistent with Qt's CSS parser\n# https://bugreports.qt.io/browse/QTBUG-70897\n('hsv(10%,10%,10%)', QColor.fromHsv(25, 25, 25)),\n```\n\nThis indicates the bug is actually consistent with Qt's CSS parser implementation (Qt Bug QTBUG-70897), so it may be intentional compatibility behavior.\n\n## Fix Strategy (Not Implemented)\n\nTo fix this bug, the `_parse_value()` method would need to:\n\n1. Accept an optional parameter indicating the component type (hue, saturation, value, alpha, red, green, blue)\n2. Apply different scaling factors based on the component type:\n   - Hue: scale to 0-359\n   - All others: scale to 0-255\n\nAlternatively, the color parsing logic could be refactored to handle HSV percentages differently from RGB percentages, with separate parsing functions.\n\n## Test Coverage\n\nA comprehensive regression test suite has been created at `/workspace/regression_test.py` with 11 test cases covering:\n\n1. HSV percentage parsing with various percentage values (10%, 20%, 50%, 100%)\n2. HSVA percentage parsing with mixed percentages\n3. Integer HSV/HSVA values (which are unaffected)\n4. RGB percentage parsing (which works correctly despite the same scaling bug)\n5. Root cause verification of the _parse_value method\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
